Mr. President, I rise today to recognize the 75th anniversary of the Detroit Windsor Tunnel. Over the past 75 years, the tunnel has been an important transportation link between the American and Canadian states and between the United States and Canada, and has been an important border crossing for many Canadian trade and transportation officials.  The Detroit Windsor Tunnel was designed in 1930 for use by workers crossing from the U.S. to Canada by means of a hoist. In the late 1930s, the U.S. Congress agreed to build a temporary transfer hoist from the Detroit River to the tunnel so that workers could direct traffic and move goods through the tunnel by hoisting the passageway. The project continued to be a priority of the U.S. Senate until 1994, when a planned Ohio replacement was canceled. The tunnel is only accessible by bicycle from Windsor's Union Station.  The tunnel is maintained by the Department of Transportation, the Department of
